9:00 AM 
 
TIME MEETING CALLED TO ORDER: 9:01 A.M. 
 
Pursuant to §92-3.7, Hawaii Revised Statutes, the meeting was conducted as a 
remote meeting by interactive conference technology, via BlueJeans 
https://maui.bluejeans.com/295235670. 
 
In person testimony and viewing: Council Chamber, Kalana O Maui Building, 8th 
Floor, 200 S. High Street, Wailuku, Hawaii. 
 
Video recording of meeting available at: www.mauicounty.legistar.com

CR 23-109 Recommending FIRST READING of Bill 121, CD1 (2023), to amend 
the Fiscal Year 2024 Budget by: 1) amending Section 2, Estimated Revenues, by 
increasing Carryover/Savings from the General Fund by $7,403,895; 
2) amending Section 3.B.9., Department of Manageme nt, by adding a new 
program entitled “Office of Recovery” with 8.0 equivalent personnel, a Category 
A (Salaries) appropriation of $403,895, a Category B (Operations & Equipment) 
appropriation of $7,000,000, and a Total appropriation of $7,403,895; 
3) adjusting the totals accordingly; and 4) amending Appendix A, Part I, Grants 
and Restricted Uses Revenues - Schedule of Grants and Restricted Use Revenues 
by Departments and Programs for Fiscal Year 2024, by adding a new 
appropriation entitled “Private Donation s” under the Department of 
Management, in the amount of $200,000.

11:18 a.m. CR 23 -116 called and at 12:05 p.m. consideration deferred  to the 
December 22, 2023, meeting: 
CR 23-116 Recommending FIRST READING of Bill 120, CD1 (2023), to authorize 
the Mayor to enter into an intergovernmental agreement with the State 
Department of Land and Natural Resources for a management right -of-entry 
permit for parcels totaling 52.7 acres and identified for real property tax 
purposes as tax map keys (2) 4 -8-003:007 and (2) 4 -8-003:008 (portion), 
Olowalu, Maui, Hawaii, to allow for wildfire debris landfill and ancillary 
purposes. 
 
 
CR 23-105 Recommending FIRST READING of Bill 52, CD1 (2022), to require: 
1) municipal wastewater effluent discharged by the County to meet Hawaii State 
R-1 reuse water standards, 2) municipal wastewater effluent reused by the 
County to meet Environmental Protection Agency (“EPA” ) drinking water 
standards; and 3) sufficient County funding for the implementation of these 
provisions without resulting in a significant increase in residential sewage rates.

CR 23-110 Recommending FIRST READING of Bill 122, CD1 (2023), to amend 
the Fiscal Year 2024 Budget by: 1) amending Section 2, Estimated Revenues, by 
increasing Carryover/Savings from the General Fund and Interfund Transfers, 
each by $5,200,000; 2) amending Section 3.B.4.e, Department of Environmental 
Management, Solid Waste Operations Program - Solid Waste Management Fund, 
by increasing Category B (Operations & Equipment) and Total appropriations by 
$4,000,000; 3) amending Section 3.B.5.g.(6), Department of Fi nance, 
Countywide Costs, Supplemental Transfer to the Solid Waste Fund, by 
increasing Category B (Operations & Equipment) and Total appropriations by 
$5,200,000; 4) amending Section 4.A.7., Department of Environmental 
Management, West Maui Community Plan Area, to add a new appropriation for 
Sanitation, Solid Waste Management Fund, entitled “Lāhainā Wildfire Final 
Disposition Site,” in the amount of $1,200,000; 5) adjusting the totals 
accordingly; and 6) amending Appendix C - Capital Improvement Projects, 
Department of Environmental Management, West Maui Community Plan Area, 
to add a new project and project description entitled “Lāhainā Wildfire Final 
Disposition Site,” in the amount of $1,200,000.

file:///P|/OCC/LEG/Minutes/2023/231215/231215.txt[12/27/2023 12:49:42 PM]
THAT I HAVE GATHERED ABOUT THE DESIGN OF THE SITE, IT SEEMS INADEQUATE TO SAFELY 
STORE THE PROPOSED 400,000 TONS OF TOXIC WASTE, WHICH INCLUDES ARSENIC, DIOXINS, 
ASBESTOS AND OTHER EXTREMELY HARMFUL SUBSTANCES. THE PROPOSED OLOWALU SITE 
CANNOT SUFFICIENTLY CONTAIN THESE TOXINS OVER THE LONG HAUL. SO CONSIDERING FUTURE 
GENERATIONS, IT'S MY HUMBLE REQUEST THAT THIS DECISION BE POSTPONED UNTIL THE 
COMMUNITY CAN BE MORE ADEQUATELY INFORMED, AND THAT THEIR VOICES CAN BE TAKEN 
INTO CONSIDERATION. I'M ALSO ASKING FOR GREATER TRANSPARENCY AND ACCOUNTABILITY 
REGARDING THE OLOWALU SITE.\r\n\r\n>> THANK YOU. >> THANK YOU. >> MAY WE HAVE THE 
NEXT TESTIFIER. >> CHAIR, THE NEXT TESTIFIER IS LINDA, ALSO TESTIFYING ON CR23-116. >> 
ALOHA. COUNCIL MEMBERS AND COUNCIL CHAIR, THANK YOU FOR THE OPPORTUNITY TO 
EXPRESS MY OPINION ON THE MATTER OF CR23-116. MY NAME IS LINDA TAYLOR, I'M AN 
ENVIRONMENTAL CIVIL ENGINEER WITH OVER 35 YEARS' OF WASTEWATER EXPERIENCE WORKING 
ON MAUI. IN CONSIDERATION TO OUR GREAT LOSSES IN THE LAHAINA TRAGEDY, WE NEED TO 
RESPECTFULLY REMOVE AND RELOCATE THE TOXIC DEBRIS AND ASHES IN THE MOST 
ENVIRONMENTAL SAFE AND SENSITIVE WAY WE CAN. IN MY PROFESSIONAL OPINION, THERE 
NEEDS TO BE TRANSPARENCY AND DETAILED PLANNING WITH THE COMMUNITY INPUT, THE 
OLOWALU SITE IS UNIQUE GEOGRAPHIC AND LIES ABOVE OUR AQUIFER LENS AND CLOSE 
PROXIMITY TO THE OCEAN IS CONCERNS AS MAUI STORMWATER RUN-OFF ALREADY DISCHARGES 
INTO THE OCEAN AROUND US.\r\n\r\nWE'RE CURRENTLY EXPERIENCING REEF DAMAGE AND 
UNCLEAN WATER QUALITY DUE TO STORM RUN-OFF FROM SEDIMENTS AND NUTRIENTS AND 
LEACHATE WILL HAVE A DAMAGING EVERYTHING ON OUR MARINE ENVIRONMENT. THIS IS NOT A 
COOKIE-CUTTER SOLUTION AND REQUIRES OUR UNIQUE ISLAND ENVIRONMENT TO BE TAKEN 
INTO CONSIDERATION. OUR DRINKING WATER ONCE OUR DRINKING WATER RECREATIONAL

BY MEMBER SUGIMURA. AND DISCUSSION, MEMBER COOK. >> THANK YOU, MEMBERS. YOUR 
WATER AND INFRASTRUCTURE COMMITTEE MET ON NOVEMBER 13TH, AND NOVEMBER 27TH, 2023 
TO DISCUSS BILL 42 (2023). BILL 42'S PURPOSE IS TO ENABLE THE CREATION OF SEPARATE LOTS 
WITHIN THE SUBDIVISION FOR THE PRESERVATION OF HISTORIC PROPERTIES. YOUR COMMITTEE 
FINDS THAT THE HISTORIC PRESERVATION LOTS MUST BE CONVEYED TO EITHER AN ACCREDITED 
LAND ORGANIZATION, OR A GOVERNMENT AGENCY TO ENSURE THAT THE HISTORIC PROPERTIES 
ARE PROPERLY AND RESPONSIBLY PROTECTED AND PRESERVED. AFTER WORKING WITH THE 
DEPARTMENT OF PLANNING, AND PUBLIC WORKS, AND THE COUNTY PRINCIPAL ARCHAEOLOGIST, 
WE PROPOSED A REVISED VERSION OF BILL 42. THE DEPARTMENT OF ENVIRONMENTAL 
MANAGEMENT, FIRE AND PUBLIC SAFETY, AND THE WATER SUPPLY -- ONE AMENDING THE BILL'S 
TITLE, TWO, CLARIFYING THAT THE LAND TRUST ORGANIZATION MUST BE ACCREDITED BY THE 
LAND TRUST ACCREDITATION COMMISSION, FOR EXAMPLE, HAWAIIAN ISLANDS LAND TRUST, 
KNOWN AS HILT. THE TRUST FOR PUBLIC LANDS, TPL, ARE ACCREDITED ORGANIZATIONS IN 
HAWAI'I. CLARIFYING THE REQUIREMENTS FOR LANDS ELIGIBLE FOR INCLUSION IN THE HISTORIC 
PRESERVATION LOT, AND 4, CLARIFYING THAT AMENITIES AND IMPROVEMENTS MAY BE 
ALLOWED RATHER THAN REQUIRED.\r\n\r\nALTHOUGH THERE WERE CONCERNS ABOUT THE 
FINANCIAL OBLIGATIONS FOR MAINTAINING THE LOTS, INTERNAL REVENUE SERVICE CODE 
SECTION 501(C)(3) REQUIRES ASSETS TO BE TRANSFERRED TO ANOTHER ORGANIZATION WITH 
SIMILAR PURPOSES IF AN ORGANIZATION DISSOLVES. FURTHER, THE LAND TRUST ACCREDITATION  
COMMISSION REQUIRES PERIODIC FINANCIAL REPORTING TO MEET ACCREDITATION 
REQUIREMENTS YOUR COMMITTEE FINDS THAT THE BILL WOULD HELP TO FURTHER SEVERAL 
MAUI COUNTY GENERAL PLAN OBJECTIVES, AND POLICIES. TO FURTHER PROTECTION HISTORIC 
AND CULTURAL RESOURCES AND SITES. YOUR COMMITTEE VOTED 8-1 TO RECOMMEND PASSAGE 
OF BILL 41, CD 1 ON FIRST READING. I RESPECTFULLY ASK FOR THE MEMBERS' SUPPORT FOR MY 
MOTIONS. >> ANY MORE DISCUSSION? MEMBER RAWLINS-FERNANDEZ.\r\n\r\n>> MAHALO, CHAIR.
